Sometimes the ideas that change your life don’t show up with fireworks. They show up in a quiet moment… in a journal… right before breakfast.

TOMS started as a scribble on a page. A simple thought: what if business could give just as much as it sold?

And then life rushed back in… friends knocking on the door, polo matches to get to, real life happening all around me… but that little idea wouldn’t leave me alone.

A month later we were stuffing 250 pairs of shoes into duffel bags and hauling them back to LA.

Big missions can begin in the most ordinary moments. You just have to pay attention to the ones that tug at you.

[58] post_id=3850683428556078654 timestamp=2026-03-11T19:27:37.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/DVwYC0tkX4-/
I’ve always been known as the optimist.
Positive. Driven. Always moving forward.

That energy carried me through tennis, business, and building TOMS. For years, my life was full of purpose, momentum, and meaning. There was always another mission. Another place to be. Another reason to wake up fired up.

Then I sold TOMS.

The pace slowed. The noise stopped. We moved to a quiet mountain town and suddenly there was space. Stillness. Long winters. Less sunlight.

And everything I’d been outrunning caught up to me.

What I didn’t understand then is that I had gone from constant purpose and validation to quiet and inward reflection. My nervous system didn’t know how to handle it. So I did what I’d always done. I chased adventure. Activity. Distraction.

It worked for a while. Until it didn’t.

Looking back now, I see that breakdown as a turning point. It forced me inward. It showed me that no amount of achievement could fix what was happening inside.

That’s why I’m building what I needed back then.

A reminder that we don’t have to earn our worth.

We are already ENOUGH.

#blakemycoskie #entrepreneur #positivity

[63] post_id=3847866542957113883 timestamp=2026-03-07T22:13:57.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/DVmXjvkEbIb/
This week a new team member asked me what their title should be.

My answer was simple: use whatever title helps you do the job.

I’ve never loved titles. They create pecking orders and unnecessary division. In the early days of TOMS, we let people make up their own titles.

Mine was Chief Shoe Giver. One of our interns was the Head of Sales.

Why? Because we needed Nordstrom to take the call seriously. If they said, “I’m just an intern,” the conversation was over.

Titles matter less than results. Especially in small organizations, don’t get caught up in them. Let people use whatever title helps them get the job done.

#blakemycoskie #entrepreneur #positivity

I sold TOMS in 2019.

The depression didn’t hit right away.

For years, my life ran on a constant dopamine dump.

When that stopped, my nervous system crashed.

I tried to replace the high with more intensity.

It only made the emptiness louder.

What I didn’t understand then was that I was in dopamine withdrawal.

Healing didn’t come from chasing another rush.

It came from slowing down and rebuilding my baseline.

Quiet mornings.

Sunlight.

Stillness.

Less stimulation.

That lesson is part of why @wearenough exists.

A reminder that your worth isn’t tied to intensity or achievement.

[139] post_id=3810746442227732290 timestamp=2026-01-15T16:59:57.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/DTifbLyEU9C/
Something I realized recently is that I never really let myself feel sadness.

Whenever it showed up, I stayed busy.
Moved on.
Focused forward.

After my divorce, everything felt like it was falling apart.
And for the first time, I didn’t try to fix it.

I let myself feel it.

The sadness.
The grief.
The uncertainty.

And something unexpected happened.
When I stopped fighting the sadness, I didn’t feel depressed or hopeless.

I just felt sad.

And honestly, that wasn’t so bad.

I could move through my day feeling sad, but not stuck.
Not drowning.
Not hopeless.

I’ll take sadness over hopelessness any day.

If you’re going through something heavy, you don’t have to be okay right now.
Let yourself feel it.

#blakemycoskie #positivity #mentalhealth #life

I started TOMS in 2006.

Over the next decade, we gave more than 100 million shoes to children in need.

From the outside, my life looked perfect.

From the inside, I was struggling.

After selling the company, the emptiness got louder, not quieter.

It eventually led me to the darkest moment of my life.

That moment forced me to stop chasing what I thought would fix me

and start doing the hard work of healing.

I stepped back.

I got quiet.

I learned how to sit with myself.

And slowly, I came back 

not as a founder or a public figure,

but as a human being.

Along the way, I learned the truth that saved my life:

I am enough.

Most people think happiness fades with age. The research says it returns.

Across 50 countries, scientists found life satisfaction dips in midlife, hitting its low around 47. Then it rises again with every decade after 50.

Getting older isn’t decline. It’s the quiet return of joy.

“Happiness, Stress, and Age: HOW THE U CURVE VARIES ACROSS PEOPLE AND PLACES,”JOURNAL OF POPULATION ECONOMICS, JANUARY 2017

[184] post_id=3787745252552826778 timestamp=2025-12-14T23:21:10.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/DSQxj0mFV-a/
A lot of people don’t know this, but one of my biggest entrepreneurial inspirations was my mom.

She wrote a cookbook called Butter Busters. It started with a real problem. She had high cholesterol and wanted to fix it, not just for herself, but to help other people too.

She wrote the book on a basic word processor and shared it with friends. Those friends started losing weight. Their cholesterol went down. Word spread.
She went on the road, told her story, and Butter Busters became the number one bestselling cookbook in America for multiple years, making tens of millions of dollars.

I was 15 years old watching it all happen. It was one of the greatest entrepreneurial lessons I could’ve learned.

So thank you, Mom. Your story deserves to be shared.

[198] post_id=3771668373911453647 timestamp=2025-11-22T18:58:49.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/DRXqGclkT_P/
Why am I wearing a winter coat, beanie, wetsuit and booties at night ?

The same reason I have the biggest smile on my face

I was lucky enough to be invited by my great friend Andrew Palmer to surf at @surf.ranch under the lights this week.

Surfing with friends is one of the greatest joys of my life and being back reminded me of how much my mental health has improved from 2 years ago when I was invited and had to pretend to be stoked because I felt nothing inside.

If the things that normally bring you the most joy are no longer doing that, please tell someone. It is one of the key signs that you are clinically depressed and need help. I was honest with my friends about this and they helped me get help. Please do the same. You are not trapped, healing is possible, and you are not alone

[215] post_id=3754944799972633353 timestamp=2025-10-30T17:12:03.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/DQcPmapkasJ/
I got this Tattoo after doing the Grand Traverse many summers ago.

It took us 58 hours to summit all 10 peaks and we were blessed to experience the solar eclipse during our time up there. I still cant believe that these peaks are in my backyard and try to spend as much time as i can up in them.

People ask me all the time if i will do the “traverse” again, and my answer is always the same, “only when it becomes a very important goal of a friend or family member, and if that never happens, well no”.

For me, i love 2 different experiences of mountaineering equally. 

The first is to summit something i have never done, or take a route that is new. 

And the second, which became really apparent to me last summer is the joy i get taking people up for the first time. it has been my joy and honor to spend time up there with close friends and family the past few years.

When anyone ever asks about my tattoo, i am quick to recall the memories I’ve made with people up there.

[225] post_id=3740385454022787423 timestamp=2025-10-10T15:05:50.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/DPohMDGEQFf/
Today is World Mental Health Day.

A few years ago, I was battling crippling depression and barely made it out. What I’ve learned since is that mental illness often hides in plain sight. It’s not always visible, like a broken bone, but it can be just as painful.

If someone you love starts isolating, losing interest in the things they once loved, struggling to sleep, or showing changes in their appearance or energy, check in. Ask how they’re really doing, and if they say “I’m fine,” ask again.

You never know how much your presence might mean to someone who’s silently fighting to stay afloat. 💚

[253] post_id=3684061178411474698 timestamp=2025-07-24T21:58:57.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/DMgah9uBd8K/
“Who knows?”

Two words that changed the way I live.

It’s something Alejo, my original TOMS partner and lifelong friend, says all the time. At first, it just made me laugh. But over the years, it’s become one of the deepest truths I know, so important that I tattooed it and him saying it on my forearm.

We spend so much time trying to control the future, but it is not possible and only leads to stress, anxiety, and disappointment. So next time you find yourself trying to predict what will happen or plan for every scenario possible, stop, throw your hands up, and say “who knows” out loud. My guess is you will not only get a good laugh, but also find that your stress and anxiety dissipate.

Thank you, Alejo, for being not only a best friend but one of the wisest teachers I have had the pleasure of “walking home” with.

[261] post_id=3668030925335718951 timestamp=2025-07-02T19:13:23.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/DLndrFJyGwn/
One year ago today I took this picture with my mom @pammycoskie and my “LA mom” @lizheller - two of the most important people in my life. 

There I was surrounded by those who loved me more than anything in the world and if you swipe and take a closer look you will see that we are all smiling. But underneath that smile was darkness, confusion and hopelessness. With depression, the outward appearance does not always reveal the truth within. 

As the photo was being taken, all I could think was this might be the last photo I ever take with them.  I had lost control over my mind and my thoughts raced, swirled and centered on ending my life and putting a stop to the feeling of deep despair that had taken over.  

Thanks to God, my family, friends and many different healing modalities, I got the help I needed and did not end my life. Instead, through the help of others I was able to use the depression to wake up to all the ways I had abandoned myself.  

The healings I have had this year have been 40 years in the making, and each day is a beautiful day of recovery and redemption.  

If you are feeling lost, stuck or in deep despair, do not give up. Tell a friend and ask for help.  You are not alone and you will get through it.  And some day you might even look back and say “thank you depression” thank you for being that “check engine light” to my soul.  

If you do not have anyone to talk to, please call 988 - This suicide hotline gives you 24/7 access to trained crisis counselors who provide confidential emotional support via phone, text, or online chat - helping with suicidal thoughts, emotional distress, or other mental health struggle. Or text HOME to 741741 which is a free 24/7 confidential support via text message. Your message is answered by a trained volunteer counselor who listens and provides guidance through tough times.

#mentalhealth #suicideprevention #askforhelp #moms #yourenotalone

[293] post_id=2377822094143941548 timestamp=2020-08-17T15:35:04.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/CD_uJishmus/
About 3 weeks ago I started using only a flip phone and regular camera instead of my iPhone.  Wow, what an amazing experience.  Here is what I have learned:
1.  It is SO much easier to be fully present with kids and friends 
2.  You can easily do all the text, emails, social etc on your computer or iPhone (via WiFi) at key dedicated times during day and in a dedicated space
3.  If people really need you, they will call and vice versa.  I have loved talking to people more instead of texting. Even if it is a 2 min call, it’s so great
4.  With a real camera, you don’t get distracted by anything than connecting with the moment and person you are shooting. And you feel more creative when carrying it around

Ok. I am going to stick with it for at least another month and look forward to hearing others experiences getting off their smart phones and getting back to full presence 
Carpe diem
Blake

[326] post_id=2309691280969714300 timestamp=2020-05-15T15:31:18.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/CANq_uXBEp8/
Swipe right to see what I’m seeing on my phone 😄 For the past few years I used instagram here and there but never felt an inescapable draw to it like I have the past 6 months. On one hand, I have benefited greatly from going down rabbit holes on the “gram” and have been inspired by so many strangers ability to share, not to mention discovered many new places to experience wanderlust in the real world, BUT over time I found myself being pulled out of moments and experiences to “check in”. And each time I found it harder and harder to re-engage in my regular life.
So I am trying an experiment and it is going really great:
1.  I took the instagram app off my phone
2.  I blocked the Instagram website from phone
3. I set a designated time each day to open up my iPad and use the instagram app to “check in” kind of like we used to “check the mailbox”. I have found this “instagram hour” to be even more entertaining, inspiring and fun and that I am not distracted throughout the day by what might be going on outside of my personal experience.  I hope me “sharing” this experiment with you helps you create your own personal strategy for making social work for you and not the other way around. Ok. Happy scrolling and see you tomorrow :) same place, same time. #Present #DigitalDetox

[335] post_id=2296619034621549322 timestamp=2020-04-27T14:39:05.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/B_fOtgPBJsK/
Of all things I’ve reconnected to during this time in quarantine, my love for writing poetry is at the top of the list. Here’s what I wrote this weekend:

𝙴𝚟𝚎𝚗 𝚠𝚑𝚎𝚗 𝚢𝚘𝚞 𝚌𝚊𝚗’𝚝 𝚜𝚎𝚎 𝚝𝚑𝚎 𝚜𝚝𝚊𝚛𝚜 𝚝𝚑𝚎𝚢 𝚊𝚛𝚎 𝚜𝚝𝚒𝚕𝚕 𝚝𝚑𝚎𝚛𝚎. 𝙰𝚗𝚍 𝚘𝚞𝚛 𝚙𝚊𝚝𝚝𝚎𝚛𝚗𝚜, 𝚊𝚝𝚝𝚊𝚌𝚑𝚖𝚎𝚗𝚝𝚜 𝚊𝚗𝚍 𝚏𝚎𝚊𝚛𝚜 𝚊𝚛𝚎 𝚗𝚘 𝚍𝚒𝚏𝚏𝚎𝚛𝚎𝚗𝚝 𝚝𝚑𝚊𝚗 𝚕𝚒𝚐𝚑𝚝 𝚙𝚘𝚕𝚕𝚞𝚝𝚒𝚘𝚗 𝚒𝚗 𝚝𝚑𝚎 𝚊𝚒𝚛.

𝙺𝚎𝚎𝚙𝚒𝚗𝚐 𝚞𝚜 𝚏𝚛𝚘𝚖 𝚜𝚎𝚎𝚒𝚗𝚐 𝚠𝚑𝚊𝚝 𝚠𝚎 𝚛𝚎𝚊𝚕𝚕𝚢 𝚊𝚛𝚎, 𝚠𝚑𝚊𝚝’𝚜 𝚊𝚌𝚝𝚞𝚊𝚕𝚕𝚢 𝚊𝚕𝚠𝚊𝚢𝚜 𝚝𝚑𝚎𝚛𝚎.  𝙳𝚎𝚎𝚙 𝚒𝚗 𝚘𝚞𝚛 𝚜𝚘𝚞𝚕 𝚊𝚗𝚍 𝚋𝚎𝚢𝚘𝚗𝚍 𝚘𝚞𝚛 𝚊𝚝𝚖𝚘𝚜𝚙𝚑𝚎𝚛𝚎.

𝙰 𝚌𝚒𝚝𝚢 𝚏𝚞𝚕𝚕 𝚘𝚏 𝚕𝚒𝚐𝚑𝚝𝚜 𝚒𝚜 𝚗𝚘 𝚍𝚒𝚏𝚏𝚎𝚛𝚎𝚗𝚝 𝚝𝚑𝚊𝚗 𝚊 𝚋𝚞𝚜𝚢 𝚖𝚒𝚗𝚍, 𝚌𝚘𝚗𝚜𝚝𝚊𝚗𝚝𝚕𝚢 𝚊𝚜𝚔𝚒𝚗𝚐 𝚒𝚝𝚜𝚎𝚕𝚏 𝚊𝚖 𝚒 𝚕𝚘𝚟𝚎𝚍, 𝚊𝚖 𝚒 𝚎𝚗𝚘𝚞𝚐𝚑, 𝚍𝚘 𝚒 𝚖𝚊𝚝𝚝𝚎𝚛, 𝚜𝚑𝚘𝚞𝚕𝚍 𝚒 𝚋𝚎 𝚖𝚘𝚛𝚎 𝚔𝚒𝚗𝚍.

𝚂𝚘 𝚛𝚊𝚝𝚑𝚎𝚛 𝚝𝚑𝚊𝚗 𝚝𝚛𝚢𝚒𝚗𝚐 𝚝𝚘 𝚐𝚎𝚝 𝚎𝚟𝚎𝚛𝚢𝚘𝚗𝚎 𝚒𝚗 𝚝𝚑𝚎 𝚌𝚒𝚝𝚢 𝚝𝚘 𝚝𝚞𝚛𝚗 𝚘𝚏𝚏 𝚝𝚑𝚎𝚒𝚛 𝚕𝚒𝚐𝚑𝚝. 𝙷𝚘𝚙 𝚒𝚗 𝚢𝚘𝚞𝚛 𝚌𝚊𝚛 𝚊𝚗𝚍 𝚍𝚛𝚒𝚟𝚎 𝚊𝚜 𝚕𝚘𝚗𝚐 𝚊𝚜 𝚒𝚝 𝚝𝚊𝚔𝚎𝚜 𝚞𝚗𝚝𝚒𝚕 𝚝𝚑𝚎 𝚌𝚒𝚝𝚢 𝚒𝚜 𝚗𝚘 𝚕𝚘𝚗𝚐𝚎𝚛 𝚒𝚗 𝚜𝚒𝚐𝚑𝚝.

Shay showed me how he was carving avocado seeds into “love bugs”. I was so inspired by his kindness and vision and I carry my love bug with me everywhere now, always on the lookout for the next person to help out. Thank you shay. Pass the love bug.

[344] post_id=2285770065377229722 timestamp=2020-04-12T15:24:07.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/B-4r8ORB_ua/
Whether or not you are celebrating Easter, today marks a chance for us to reflect on what resurrection truly means.  In his book The Universal Christ, Franciscan priest Richard Rohr writes “resurrection is another word for change, but particularly positive change.” I love that we are all connected by both the spirit of Jesus’s life (his radical love, humble service and boundless grace) and the promise of his death and resurrection (new life, restoration, positive change). You don’t have to be religious to see the beauty and hope in this.

A few years ago I found this carving of the face of Jesus from a single piece of wood. I was (and continue to be) struck by the connection between the face and the wood itself. It’s a beautiful representation of how all creation, both humanity and nature, are so intimately intertwined.  How the cycles of birth, life, death and rebirth define us all.  We are all – you, me, trees, the oceans, animals, the air -  in this together.  To me that interaction is truly divine.

I now keep this carving on my desk as a reminder of these truths and that while Easter might be celebrated once a year, we get to participate in and practice Easter every single day.

[345] post_id=2285168048837376406 timestamp=2020-04-11T19:28:01.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/B-2jDurBjmW/
It seems that one of the most prevailing thoughts among friends, colleagues and family members these days is a frustration, fear, or general discomfort with how much is unknown and out of their control right now.

Well, we have always feared the unknown.  That is why death is the ultimate fear, and why we try to avoid thinking about it at all costs.

So what do we do?

In the spirit of Holy Saturday, I believe this experience can help each of us realize that we are always living in a state of unknown, but we mask it with all our distractions, entertainment etc, and that can be appropriate in small amounts, but it still does not change the fact that any of us could take our last breath at any moment and it is totally out of our control. Covid-19 is forcing us to face this fact head on, and without our typical convenient distractions, it can be really uncomfortable, even scary. I am encouraging myself and others to sit with this feeling, to recognize that it is really not different than our typical reality, and to see that there is a beautiful path of freedom for those who surrender to the unknown and fully live in the present. That is my intention as we go into this weekend.
#HolySaturday #Intention #mindset

[355] post_id=2274226482564104225 timestamp=2020-03-27T17:09:04.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/B-PrO_ABQAh/
"It Goes by Too Fast"

Every parent I know has heard the same thing from older parents, who children are grown up.  They say, with subtle remorse "It goes by too fast" when seeing my little ones.  This is the #1 comment we all here, so what can we do to slow it down?

The mind is basically a time machine.  It makes sense of our life and how time "feels" by the memories it stores.  So, I have begun to believe, the more "memories" we make, ones that are permanently etched into our minds, the more we can slow down time.

We simply do not remember our daily routines, but we do remember all the "special" moments we create with our kids.  These can be big experiences like 4 days camping in the Grand Canyon, or simple ones like building a castle of legos, or playing catch every night before dinner.  The key to it all is our presence in the moment, for it is our presence that is the magic glue that takes on experience and makes it a memory.

And making memories is how we stop it from "going too fast."

[361] post_id=2269135788011076474 timestamp=2020-03-20T16:34:46.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/B99lvoPhrt6/
I got this Tattoo after doing the #grandtraverse a few summers ago. It took us 58 hours to summit all 10 peaks and we were blessed to experience the solar eclipse during our time up there. I still cant believe that these peaks are in my backyard and try to spend as much time as I can up in them. [362] post_id=2268367938623226172 timestamp=2020-03-19T15:09:12.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/B963J8xhcE8/
For the past 3 days I have been camping solo in Baja. It has been a great way to practice extreme “social distancing” but also to reflect on how when we are alone, we can actually feel more connected to each other. The coronavirus is horrible and recking havoc on so many people’s lives so I do not point out any positives suggesting the scale is not dramatically tipped towards the negative, but I will say that a deeper feeling of oneness is possible during these times when we truly see how interconnected we all are and I believe that a greater since of oneness will help solve so many of the major problems facing the human race over the long haul, and i hope that is a lasting effect after this has all passed. We desperately need it to be.  I pray that you can find deeper feelings of interconnectedness and oneness in your seclusion today.
Stay Healthy.
Stay Strong,
Blake 
#mindfulness #solidarity

[372] post_id=2253183720054177803 timestamp=2020-02-27T16:20:52.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/B9E6qfPhcAL/
My most recent musings on relationships.
.

Relationships are meant to be teachers, guides, catalyst for a deeper understanding and connection to oneself, God, to all creation. Do not look to another person or special relationship for satisfaction, inspiration, or love, but see that person as an opportunity to give love, inspire, to serve them on their journey. This is the only way to look at the relationship. And let it go when they or you feel that you have helped them as much as you can on their path, and especially let them go if you feel you are holding them back from their next stage of growth. Do not look to another for peace and joy, you must find yourself. We are the ones we have been waiting for. 
#thursdaythoughts #relationships

25 DAYS SOBER.  Thank you @athleticbrewing for the tasty non alcoholic IPA’s and for the support during my personal Sober October challenge. Here is what I have learned so far:⁣
⁣
1. I compulsively turn to alcohol to numb uncomfortable feelings like stress, boredom, frustration, etc and I NO LONGER WANT TO DO THAT⁣
⁣
2.  When I resist the temptation to use alcohol in this way, the uncomfortable feeling passes quickly and I feel really empowered, healthy, and positive ⁣
⁣
3.  Alcohol has a different place in each of our lives and it is important to respect that for everyone individually. I don’t know the role it will ply for me going forward but I know that if it ends up having a place, it will be in celebration, and with great intention. ⁣
⁣
4. Abstaining from anything is a great way to understand its power over your life and to really form a new relationship with it.  I am deeply thankful for this Sober October experience for giving me new insight on alcohol and my compulsive patterns ⁣
⁣
#soberoctober #grateful #carpediem

[518] post_id=1952733581789271997 timestamp=2019-01-09T03:20:04.000Z url=https://www.instagram.com/p/BsZgNi7hpe9/
Today, Congress introduced a bill to require universal background checks for gun sales, so we thought we’d clear the air on what universal background checks are: 
While background checks are required for guns sold by *licensed* dealers, private sales including gun shows, online and other direct selling methods currently allow buyers to bypass the background check process, a loophole statistically shown to increase the likelihood of gun violence. 
Universal background checks are also something more than 90% of Americans agree on. 
What can you do? Take 30 seconds to go to TOMS.com and send your Representative a postcard demanding they pass this bill. 
Then, get 4 friends to do the same – one for each of the 4 Americans taken by gun violence every hour. #endgunviolencetogether

I was so inspired when I learned about the passion and determination of the national women’s soccer team in Haiti– a country that holds a special place in my heart. Investing in them through sports is a great way to create hope and opportunity. Although CONCACAF covers some costs, the donation will fund the team's financial obligations during the tournament, including transportation to and from the games, warm-ups, jackets, athletic bags, eyewear and shoes. Please join me in congratulating them on their first win and cheering them on again today as they go for a coveted spot on the 2015 World Cup Schedule.
